### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed map lists both files under the same generic skill-entrypoint role although they do opposite jobs, the reference map is a navigation instrument consumed before reading and the research brief is a provenance disclosure consumed when checking claims
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map's own opening line says use this file to route quickly before loading the full Python references, while the brief's opening line dates the skill's preparation to 2026-06-23 and names its documentation basis, two self-declared and incompatible roles
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the four external URL rows repeat the bundle-wide doc-site set with sourced-fact labels although this evolution retrieved none of them, and the brief itself names twelve further primary links the seed table omits entirely
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table records provenance for this document's claims, it does not certify that the brief's sixteen links still resolve or still say what they said in 2026

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map's Section Search block gives rg lines that enumerate live headings in both destination references and grep for the scoreboard and gate anchors, and comparing that live output against the map's own Jump Points is a mechanical staleness test for the router itself
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the rg lines assume the archive layout, they reference references/ relative paths that only resolve from the bundle root, run from anywhere else they silently return nothing and a naive reader concludes the sections are gone

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide offers the generic adopt-adapt-avoid rows without this theme's live tension, routing overhead versus reading waste, every minute spent consulting the router is pure cost on tasks where the destination was already obvious
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map prices its own overhead low, three steps and 28 lines, because it is betting against a much larger waste, full-reference context loads, and that bet only pays when the task's destination is genuinely uncertain
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: mandatory routing on trivially-routed tasks teaches contributors to fake the trace, journals fill with pro-forma scoreboard citations for sessions that never opened it, corrupting the very records the anti-pattern detection needs
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this guide tunes when routing ceremony applies, it does not license skipping the closing gate anchors, which the Use Order couples to every session regardless
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the overhead-waste axis with tiered defaults, full three-step routing for unfamiliar boundaries, direct section access with a logged skip for boundaries the operator has routed before
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that routing value concentrates in the first sessions with any boundary and decays with familiarity, but the map's freshness risk moves opposite, growing over time, so veterans who earned the right to skip routing are exactly the readers most exposed to silent map drift

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed hierarchy names the map canonical and the brief supporting but leaves the precedence question unanswered for the one conflict that matters, what wins when the map's jump points and the live reference headings disagree
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map is a derived index over the two destination references, its authority is entirely borrowed, so on any content disagreement the destination files win by construction and the map is simply stale
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: calling the map canonical invites the inverted reading, trusting the index over the indexed, a reader who cannot find a jump-point section may conclude the content was removed when only the pointer rotted
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this hierarchy settles precedence among the two mapped files and their destinations, precedence among the destination references themselves belongs to their own themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to declare the destination references canonical for content, the map canonical only for reading order, and the brief canonical only for preparation-time provenance
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that each file in this hierarchy is unfalsifiable on exactly one axis, the brief can never be wrong about what it lists, the map can never be wrong about what order it prescribes, conflicts are only possible where a file speaks beyond its axis
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to resolve any map-versus-destination mismatch by trusting the destination and filing the mismatch as router drift to repair
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the map is a derived index over the two destination references, its authority is entirely borrowed, so on any content disagreement the destination files win by construction and the map is simply stale
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; calling the map canonical invites the inverted reading, trusting the index over the indexed, a reader who cannot find a jump-point section may conclude the content was removed when only the pointer rotted
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this hierarchy settles precedence among the two mapped files and their destinations, precedence among the destination references themselves belongs to their own themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: declare the destination references canonical for content, the map canonical only for reading order, and the brief canonical only for preparation-time provenance
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies each file in this hierarchy is unfalsifiable on exactly one axis, the brief can never be wrong about what it lists, the map can never be wrong about what order it prescribes, conflicts are only possible where a file speaks beyond its axis

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed artifact table asks for abstract routing rules while the mapped files compose directly into a concrete object, a routing card that pairs each jump point with its live heading check and each claim class with its brief citation line
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every element of such a card is verbatim bundle content, eight jump points, three rg commands, three use-order steps, and the brief's link groups, only the last-verified date requires per-checkout instantiation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a routing card without its verification date is worse than none, it propagates the map's pointers with an added layer of authority while dropping the one field that flags staleness
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the card standardizes routed entry into this bundle, it does not replace the map file, which stays the reference of record the card is derived from
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the artifact as the dated routing card, jump points with heading-check results, the three-step order, and the brief's claim-class citation key
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the card's date field turns router freshness from a trust question into an arithmetic one, any reader can compare card date against bundle file modification dates and know instantly whether re-verification is owed

## Section 014: Worked Example Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed examples describe reference usage abstractly while the mapped files support a concrete end-to-end walkthrough, one task routed through all three use-order steps with a provenance challenge answered from the brief at the end
- **supporting_reason:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map's steps are demonstration-shaped, a walkthrough needs only a realistic task, a cancellation bug say, to show the scoreboard read, the single-section match on async and resource reliability, the closing anti-pattern check, and the brief lookup when asked why cancellation guidance is trustworthy
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: single-happy-path walkthroughs mislead about the fallback, learners also need the miss case, a task matching no jump point, resolved by the rg search rather than by opening everything, or the fallback never becomes habit
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: worked examples here teach routing and provenance mechanics, examples of applying the routed content belong to the destination themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to anchor the section on two walkthroughs, a hit case routed in three steps with a brief-backed provenance answer, and a miss case resolved through the rg fallback
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the miss case teaches more than the hit case, the moment a jump point fails is where readers choose between the rg fallback and the context dump, and one rehearsed miss inoculates against the dump better than any rule statement
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed metrics name a coverage indicator but no loop connects routing outcomes back to the router, nothing counts which jump points get used, which rg fallbacks fire, or how often provenance challenges find the brief sufficient
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routed sessions generate classifiable events for free, each session has a matched-or-missed jump point, a fallback-used flag, and occasionally a provenance-challenge outcome, and tallying them shows exactly where the router earns or fails
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: usage tallies mislead without task-mix context, a never-used jump point may mark dead weight or simply a boundary the team has not touched this quarter, raw counts need the task distribution beside them
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this loop tunes the router and the ledger, it does not measure destination content quality, which the destination themes own
- **revision_decision:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the routing tally loop, per-jump-point match counts, fallback firings, and provenance-challenge outcomes, reviewed quarterly against the quarter's task mix
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that fallback firings are the loop's sharpest signal, every rg-fallback event names a section readers needed that the jump list lacks, making the miss log a ready-made backlog for the map's next revision

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model budgets one audience and twelve source documents, an authoring workload, while this theme's operational unit is the routing decision, seconds of overhead applied at the start of every bundle session, plus a rarer refresh cycle when the map is re-verified
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map is sized for that economics, 28 lines readable in under a minute, its design assumes it will be consulted hundreds of times and must cost almost nothing each time, while the brief is consulted rarely and can afford its greater length
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the model breaks when routing decisions queue, a batch of twenty heterogeneous tasks routed in one sitting degrades to jump-list skimming by the tenth, routing quality is per-decision attention and cannot be amortized across a batch
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this model budgets routing and refresh effort for bundle consumers, authoring effort for this corpus document is a separate, rarer workload
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate capacity in routing terms, one routing decision per task at negligible marginal cost, one card refresh per bundle change at minutes of cost, batch routing capped before attention decays
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that routing is the rare workload whose per-use cost rounds to zero while its skip cost does not, the asymmetry means the budget question is never can we afford to route but only how to keep the near-free habit from being dropped

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed targets measure document properties like label preservation while the router's own reliability question goes unstated, how often does a routed session land on the wrong section, and how often does the map's jump list disagree with the live headings it points at
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a router's worth is its misroute rate and its pointer accuracy, the eight jump points and three commands define the accuracy claim precisely, and every routed session's outcome is observable in the journal trace it leaves
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: misroute measurement needs honest miss reporting, an operator who quietly recovers from a wrong section and logs the session as clean erases the signal, low-blame journaling is a precondition for any of these numbers meaning anything
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: targets here cover router operation and pointer accuracy, content correctness at the destinations is measured by the destination themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the operational targets, zero stale jump points at every card refresh, and misroutes triaged within the week to either a map defect or an operator error
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the two targets police each other, a clean pointer audit with a rising misroute rate isolates the fault in routing skill, a failing pointer audit excuses the operators, so tracking both turns any failure into an attributable one

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guidance covers document-verification retries but not routing retry policy, what a reader does after landing on a wrong section, how many re-routes a task gets, and when repeated routing failures stop being noise and start indicting the map
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map has a built-in retry ladder the seed never names, a failed jump point falls back to the rg section search, a failed search falls back to escalation, and each rung is cheaper than the context dump that tempts frustrated readers
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: unbounded re-routing converges on reading everything one section at a time, which is the context dump with extra steps, two failed routes on one task is the signal to stop routing and question whether the task's boundary was misidentified
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this section governs the routing retry loop, retry policy for code and for corpus generation belongs to the gates and evolution themes respectively
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the routing retry ladder, jump point, then rg search, then boundary re-diagnosis, capped at two re-routes before escalating, with every fallback firing logged for the metrics loop
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that each rung of the ladder failing carries diagnostic weight the retry itself does not, a jump-point miss suggests map staleness, an rg miss suggests the content genuinely is not there, and a boundary re-diagnosis suggests the task was never routable as stated

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed method demands a ten-minute next-action ceiling for the document while the routing operation's performance question is sharper, seconds from task to section shortlist, and whether routing overhead stays small enough that nobody is tempted to skip it
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map's entire justification is a time trade, under a minute of routing against the minutes or context-window cost of unrouted reading, so measuring both sides of that trade is measuring whether the instrument works at all
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: optimizing routing latency alone invites hollow speed, a three-second route that lands wrong costs more than a ninety-second route that lands right, latency numbers are only interpretable beside the misroute ledger
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this method verifies the routing operation's performance, performance of the destination guidance in running code belongs to the reliability theme's own verification methods
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to measure route time from task pickup to section shortlist and reading footprint as sections opened versus sections the map named, reading both beside the misroute rate

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement bounds document scale but not the router's scaling seams, one map serving one bundle, a jump list that stays legible only while it stays short, and a single ledger whose preparation date ages for everyone at once
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the map works because eight destinations fit in one glance and 28 lines cost nothing to consult, both properties are functions of bundle size, and the brief works because one preparation event covered the whole bundle, a property that breaks the first time references are revised independently
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: scaling by growing the jump list defeats the instrument, a forty-entry jump list is a table of contents that must itself be searched, past some size the flat list must become a routed hierarchy or split into per-area maps
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this statement marks where this theme's guidance stops, corpus-wide routing across many bundles is the corpus's own indexing problem, not this file's
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the seams, jump lists beyond roughly a dozen entries need hierarchy, independently-revised references need per-file provenance dates, and multi-bundle estates need a router of routers this file does not provide
